<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Zoophilia</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

</div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E6%98%A5%E5%AE%AB%E5%86%8C%E9%A1%B5%E3%80%8A%E5%A5%B3%E4%BA%BA%E5%92%8C%E7%8B%97%E3%80%8B.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Ukiyo-e" title="Ukiyo-e">ukiyo-e</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodblock_print" title="Woodblock print">woodblock print</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kunisada" title="Kunisada">Utagawa Kunisada</a>'s series, "Eight Canine Heroes of the House of Satomi", 1837.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indiaerotic5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1573" data-file-width="2203" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Indiaerotic5.jpg/350px-Indiaerotic5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Indiaerotic5.jpg/525px-Indiaerotic5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Indiaerotic5.jpg/700px-Indiaerotic5.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indiaerotic5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An 18th-century Indian miniature depicting women practising zoophilia in the bottom register.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Zoophilia</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilia</a> involving a sexual fixation on non-human animals. <b>Bestiality</b> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross-species_sex" title="Cross-species sex">cross-species sexual activity</a> between <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> and non-human <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animals" title="Animals">animals</a>. The terms are often used interchangeably, but some researchers make a distinction between the attraction (zoophilia) and the act (bestiality).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranger_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-ranger-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia_and_the_law" title="Zoophilia and the law">sex with animals is not outlawed</a> in some countries, in most countries, bestiality is illegal under <a href="/wiki/Cruelty_to_animals" title="Cruelty to animals">animal abuse</a> laws or laws dealing with <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_nature" title="Crime against nature">crimes against nature</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h3>
<p>Three key terms commonly used in regards to the subject — <i>zoophilia</i>, <i>bestiality</i>, and <i>zoosexuality</i> — are often used somewhat interchangeably. Some researchers distinguish between zoophilia (as a persistent sexual interest in animals) and bestiality (as sexual acts with animals), because bestiality is often not driven by a sexual preference for animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranger_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ranger-1">[1]</a></sup> Some studies have found that a preference for animals is rare among people who engage in sexual contact with animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earls_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-earls-2">[2]</a></sup> Furthermore, some zoophiles report that they have never had sexual contact with an animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> People with zoophilia are known as "zoophiles", though also sometimes as "zoosexuals", or even very simply "zoos".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranger_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-ranger-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbookth_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Handbookth-4">[4]</a></sup> Zooerasty, <a href="/wiki/Sodomy" title="Sodomy">sodomy</a>, and zooerastia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> are other terms closely related to the subject but are less synonymous with the former terms, and are seldom used. "Bestiosexuality" was discussed briefly by Allen (1979), but never became widely established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bornemann" title="Ernest Bornemann">Ernest Bornemann</a> (1990, cited by Rosenbauer, 1997) coined the separate term <i><a href="/wiki/Zoosadism" title="Zoosadism">zoosadism</a></i> for those who derive pleasure – sexual or otherwise – from inflicting pain on animals. Zoosadism specifically is one member of the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_triad" title="Macdonald triad">Macdonald triad</a> of precursors to <a href="/wiki/Psychopathy" title="Psychopathy">sociopathic behavior</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacDonald_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonald-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoophilia">Zoophilia</span></h3>
<p>The term <i>zoophilia</i> was introduced into the field of research on sexuality in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychopathia_Sexualis" title="Psychopathia Sexualis">Psychopathia Sexualis</a></i> (1886) by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Freiherr_von_Krafft-Ebing" title="Richard Freiherr von Krafft-Ebing">Krafft-Ebing</a>, who described a number of cases of "violation of animals (bestiality)",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> as well as "zoophilia erotica",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> which he defined as a sexual attraction to animal skin or fur. The term <i>zoophilia</i> derives from the combination of two nouns in <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <i><b>ζῷον</b></i> (<i>zṓion</i>, meaning "animal") and <i><b>φιλία</b></i> (<i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-philia" title="wiktionary:-philia">philia</a></i>, meaning "(fraternal) love"). In general contemporary usage, the term <i>zoophilia</i> may refer to sexual activity between human and non-human animals, the desire to engage in such, or to the specific <a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilia</a> (<i>i.e.,</i> the atypical arousal) which indicates a definite preference for non-human animals over humans as sexual partners. Although Krafft-Ebing also coined the term <i>zooerasty</i> for the paraphilia of exclusive sexual attraction to animals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deviance_391_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-deviance_391-9">[9]</a></sup> that term has fallen out of general use.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoosexuality">Zoosexuality</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1116" data-file-width="1600" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg/220px-Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg/330px-Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg/440px-Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tako_to_ama_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katsushika_Hokusai" title="Katsushika Hokusai">Hokusai</a>'s (1760–1849) <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dream_of_the_Fisherman%27s_Wife" title="The Dream of the Fisherman's Wife">The Dream of the Fisherman's Wife</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The term <i>zoosexual</i> was proposed by <a href="/wiki/Hani_Miletski" title="Hani Miletski">Hani Miletski</a> in 2002<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbookth_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Handbookth-4">[4]</a></sup> as a value-neutral term. Usage of <i>zoosexual</i> as a noun (in reference to a person) is synonymous with zoophile, while the adjectival form of the word – as, for instance, in the phrase "zoosexual act" – may indicate sexual activity between a human and a non-human animal. The derivative noun "zoosexuality" is sometimes used by self-identified zoophiles in both support groups and on internet-based discussion forums to designate <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> manifesting as romantic or emotional involvement with, or sexual attraction to, non-human animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbookth_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Handbookth-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bestiality">Bestiality</span></h3>
<p>The legal term <i>bestiality</i> has two common pronunciations: "ˌbɛs'tiæ'lə'ti" or "ˌbis'tiæ'lə'ti", the latter being more prevalent in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Some zoophiles and researchers draw a distinction between <i>zoophilia</i> and <i>bestiality</i>, using the former to describe the desire to form sexual relationships with animals, and the latter to describe the sex acts alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Confusing the matter yet further, writing in 1962, Masters used the term <i>bestialist</i> specifically in his discussion of zoosadism.</p>
<p>Stephanie LaFarge, an assistant professor of psychiatry at the New Jersey Medical School, and Director of Counseling at the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_for_the_Prevention_of_Cruelty_to_Animals" title="American Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Animals">ASPCA</a>, writes that two groups can be distinguished: bestialists, who rape or abuse animals, and zoophiles, who form an emotional and sexual attachment to animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colin_J._Williams" title="Colin J. Williams">Colin J. Williams</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Weinberg" title="Martin Weinberg">Martin Weinberg</a> studied self-defined zoophiles via the internet and reported them as understanding the term <i>zoophilia</i> to involve concern for the animal's welfare, pleasure, and consent, as distinct from the self-labelled zoophiles' concept of "bestialists", whom the zoophiles in their study defined as focused on their own gratification. Williams and Weinberg also quoted a British newspaper saying that <i>zoophilia</i> is a term used by "apologists" for <i>bestiality</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent_of_occurrence">Extent of occurrence</span></h2>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kinsey_report" title="Kinsey report">Kinsey reports</a> rated the percentage of people who had sexual interaction with animals at some point in their lives as 8% for men and 3.6% for women, and claimed it was 40–50% in people living near farms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deviance_391_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-deviance_391-9">[9]</a></sup> but some later writers dispute the figures, because the study lacked a random sample in that it included a disproportionate number of prisoners, causing <a href="/wiki/Sampling_bias" title="Sampling bias">sampling bias</a>. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Duberman" title="Martin Duberman">Martin Duberman</a> has written that it is difficult to get a random sample in sexual research, and that even when <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gebhard" title="Paul Gebhard">Paul Gebhard</a>, Kinsey's research successor, removed prison samples from the figures, he found the figures were not significantly changed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1974, the farm population in the USA had declined by 80 percent compared with 1940, reducing the opportunity to live with animals; Hunt's 1974 study suggests that these demographic changes led to a significant change in reported occurrences of bestiality. The percentage of males who reported sexual interactions with animals in 1974 was 4.9% (1948: 8.3%), and in females in 1974 was 1.9% (1953: 3.6%). Miletski believes this is not due to a reduction in interest but merely a reduction in opportunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nancy_Friday" title="Nancy Friday">Nancy Friday</a>'s 1973 book on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Female_sexuality" title="Female sexuality">female sexuality</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Secret_Garden" title="My Secret Garden">My Secret Garden</a></i>, comprised around 190 fantasies from different women; of these, 23 involve zoophilic activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In one study, psychiatric patients were found to have a statistically significant higher prevalence rate (55 percent) of reported bestiality, both actual sexual contacts (45 percent) and sexual fantasy (30 percent) than the control groups of medical in-patients (10 percent) and psychiatric staff (15 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psych_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-psych-18">[18]</a></sup> Crépault and Couture (1980) reported that 5.3 percent of the men they surveyed had fantasized about sexual activity with an animal during heterosexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In a 2014 study, 3% of women and 2.2% of men reported fantasies about having sex with an animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> A 1982 study suggested that 7.5 percent of 186 university students had interacted sexually with an animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Faunoiphilia"></span> Sexual arousal from watching animals mate is known as <i>faunoiphilia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> A frequent interest in and sexual excitement at watching animals <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">mate</a> is cited as an indicator of latent zoophilia by Massen (1994). <a href="/wiki/Sexual_fantasy" title="Sexual fantasy">Sexual fantasies</a> about zoophilic acts can occur in people who do not have any wish to experience them in real life. Nancy Friday notes that zoophilia as a fantasy may provide an escape from cultural expectations, restrictions, and judgements in regard to sex. Masters (1962) says that some brothel madams used to stage exhibitions of animals mating, as they found it aroused potential clientele, and that this may have encouraged the clients to engage in bestiality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watching_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-watching-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup>. Several studies have found that women show stronger vaginal responses to films depicting <a href="/wiki/Bonobo#Sexual_social_behavior" title="Bonobo">bonobo copulation</a> than to non-sexual stimuli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Perspectives_on_zoophilia">Perspectives on zoophilia</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="800" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg/260px-Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg/390px-Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg/520px-Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Franz_von_Bayros_020.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Art by <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Bayros" title="Franz von Bayros">Franz von Bayros</a> depicting <a href="/wiki/Oral_sex" title="Oral sex">oral sex</a> between an adolescent and a <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_perspectives">Research perspectives</span></h3>
<p>Zoophilia has been partly discussed by several sciences: <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a> (the study of the human <a href="/wiki/Mind" title="Mind">mind</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sexology" title="Sexology">sexology</a> (a relatively new discipline primarily studying <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">human sexuality</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">ethology</a> (the study of <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">animal behavior</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Anthrozoology" title="Anthrozoology">anthrozoology</a> (the study of human-animal interactions and bonds).</p>
<p>The nature of animal minds, animal <a href="/wiki/Mental_process" title="Mental process">mental processes</a> and structures, and animal <a href="/wiki/Self-awareness" title="Self-awareness">self-awareness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emotion_in_animals" title="Emotion in animals">emotion in animals</a>, and "map of the world", are studied within <a href="/wiki/Animal_cognition" title="Animal cognition">animal cognition</a> and also explored within various specialized branches of <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Neuroethology" title="Neuroethology">neuroethology</a>.</p>
<p>In the fifth edition of the <a href="/wiki/Diagnostic_and_Statistical_Manual_of_Mental_Disorders" title="Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders">Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders</a> (DSM-5), zoophilia is placed in the classification "other specified paraphilic disorder"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSM_5_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSM_5-26">[26]</a></sup> ("<a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilias</a> not otherwise specified" in the DSM-III and IV<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSM_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSM-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milner2008_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milner2008-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lovemaps_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lovemaps-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seto2000_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Seto2000-30">[30]</a></sup>). The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> takes the same position, listing a sexual preference for animals in its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICD" title="ICD">ICD</a><a href="/wiki/ICD-10" title="ICD-10">-10</a> as "other disorder of sexual preference".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In the DSM-5, it rises to the level of a diagnosable disorder only when accompanied by distress or interference with normal functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSM_5_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-DSM_5-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zoophilia may also be covered to some degree by other fields such as ethics, philosophy, law, <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_welfare" title="Animal welfare">animal welfare</a>. It may also be touched upon by <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> which looks both at zoosadism in examining patterns and issues related to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> and at non-sexual zoophilia in examining the role of animals as emotional support and companionship in human lives, and may fall within the scope of <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">psychiatry</a> if it becomes necessary to consider its significance in a clinical context. The Journal of Forensic and Legal Medicine (Vol. 18, February 2011) states that sexual contact with animals is almost never a clinically significant problem by itself;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scidirectpii_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-scidirectpii-33">[33]</a></sup> it also states that there are several kinds of zoophiles:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scidirectpii_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-scidirectpii-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<table>
<tr>
<td>
<div style="margin-left: 2em">
<ol start="1">
<li>Human-animal role-players</li>
<li>Romantic zoophiles</li>
<li>Zoophilic fantasizers</li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
<td>
<div style="margin-left: 2em">
<ol start="4">
<li>Tactile zoophiles</li>
<li>Fetishistic zoophiles</li>
<li>Sadistic bestials</li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
<td>
<div style="margin-left: 2em">
<ol start="7">
<li>Opportunistic zoophiles</li>
<li>Regular zoophiles</li>
<li>Exclusive zoophiles</li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Additionally, zoophiles in categories 2, 3, and 8 (romantic zoophiles, zoophilic fantasizers, and regular zoophiles) are the most common, while zoophiles found in categories 6 and 7 (sadistic bestials and opportunistic zoophiles) are the least common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scidirectpii_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-scidirectpii-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zoophilia may reflect childhood experimentation, sexual abuse or lack of other avenues of sexual expression. Exclusive desire for animals rather than humans is considered a rare paraphilia, and sufferers often have other paraphilias<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LawsO.27Donohue2008_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-LawsO.27Donohue2008-34">[34]</a></sup> with which they present. Zoophiles will not usually seek help for their condition, and so do not come to the attention of psychiatrists for zoophilia itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roukema2008_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roukema2008-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first detailed studies of zoophilia date from prior to 1910. Peer reviewed research into zoophilia in its own right started around 1960. However, a number of the most oft-quoted studies, such as Miletski, were not published in <a href="/wiki/Peer_review" title="Peer review">peer-reviewed</a> journals. There have been several significant modern books, from Masters (1962) to Beetz (2002);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz2002_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz2002-36">[36]</a></sup> their research arrived at the following conclusions:</p>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>Most zoophiles have (or have also had) long term human relationships as well or at the same time as zoosexual ones, and that zoosexual partners are usually dogs and/or horses (Masters, Miletski, Beetz)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz2002_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz2002-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggrawal2008_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aggrawal2008-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>Zoophiles' emotions and care for animals can be real, relational, authentic and (within animals' abilities) reciprocal, and not just a substitute or means of expression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Beetz believes zoophilia is not an inclination which is chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz2002_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz2002-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>Society in general at present is considerably misinformed about zoophilia, its stereotypes, and its meaning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz2002_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz2002-36">[36]</a></sup> The distinction between zoophilia and zoosadism is a critical one to these researchers, and is highlighted by each of these studies. Masters (1962), Miletski (1999) and Weinberg (2003) each comment significantly on the social harm caused by misunderstandings regarding zoophilia: "This destroy[s] the lives of many citizens".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz2002_36-4"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz2002-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>Beetz also states the following:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"The phenomenon of sexual contact with animals is starting to lose its taboo: it is appearing more often in scholarly publications, and the public are being confronted with it, too.[...] Sexual contact with animals – in the form of bestiality or zoophilia – needs to be discussed more openly and investigated in more detail by scholars working in disciplines such as animal ethics, animal behavior, anthrozoology, psychology, mental health, sociology, and the law."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeetzPodberseck_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-BeetzPodberseck-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>More recently, research has engaged three further directions – the speculation that at least some animals seem to enjoy a zoophilic relationship assuming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sadism_and_Masochism" title="Sadism and Masochism">sadism</a> is not present, and can form an affectionate bond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Similar findings are also reported by Kinsey (cited by Masters), and others earlier in history. Miletski (1999) notes that information on sex with animals on the internet is often very emphatic as to what the zoophile believes gives pleasure and how to identify what is perceived as <a href="/wiki/Consent" title="Consent">consent</a> beforehand. For instance, Jonathan Balcombe says animals do things for pleasure. But he himself says pet owners will be unimpressed by this statement, as this is not news to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beetz described the phenomenon of zoophilia/bestiality as being somewhere between crime, paraphilia and love, although she says that most research has been based on <a href="/wiki/Criminology" title="Criminology">criminological</a> reports, so the cases have frequently involved violence and psychiatric illness. She says only a few recent studies have taken data from volunteers in the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> As with all volunteer surveys and sexual ones in particular, these studies have a potential for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-selection" title="Self-selection">self-selection</a> bias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slade2001_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slade2001-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Medical research suggests that some zoophiles only become aroused by a specific species (such as horses), some zoophiles become aroused by multiple species (which may or may not include humans), and some zoophiles are not attracted to humans at all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earls_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-earls-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_and_cultural_perspectives">Historical and cultural perspectives</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="416" data-file-width="346" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg/200px-Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg/300px-Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Judensau_from_Frankfurt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The taboo of zoophilia has led to stigmatised groups being accused of it, as with <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">blood libel</a>. This German illustration shows <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> performing bestiality on a <i><a href="/wiki/Judensau" title="Judensau">Judensau</a></i>, while Satan watches.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_and_cultural_perspectives_on_zoophilia" title="Historical and cultural perspectives on zoophilia">Historical and cultural perspectives on zoophilia</a></div>
<p>Instances of this behavior have been found in the Bible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aggrawal_2009_16_3_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-aggrawal_2009_16_3-45">[45]</a></sup> In a cave painting from at least 8000 BC in the Northern Italian <a href="/wiki/Val_Camonica" title="Val Camonica">Val Camonica</a> a man is shown about to penetrate an animal. Raymond Christinger interprets that as a show of power of a tribal chief,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> and so we do not know if this practice was then more acceptable, and if the scene depicted was usual or unusual or whether it was symbolic or imaginary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bevan2006_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan2006-47">[47]</a></sup> The Cambridge Illustrated History of Prehistoric Art says the scene may be humorous, as the penetrating man seems to be waving cheerfully with his hand at the same time. Potters seem to have spent time depicting the practice, but this may be because they found the idea amusing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bahn1998_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bahn1998-48">[48]</a></sup> Dr "Jacobus X", said to be a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nom-de-plume" title="Nom-de-plume">nom-de-plume</a> for a French author, said this was clearly "before any known taboos against sex with animals existed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Marc Epprecht states that authors such as Jacobus X do not deserve respect because their methodology is based on hearsay, and was designed for voyeuristic titillation of the reader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Masters said that since pre-historic man is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric" title="Prehistoric">prehistoric</a> it goes without saying that we know little of his sexual behaviour,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> depictions in cave paintings may only show the artist's subjective preoccupations or thoughts.</p>
<p>Pindar, Herodotus, and Plutarch claimed the Egyptians engaged in ritual congress with goats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BulloughBullough1994_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-BulloughBullough1994-52">[52]</a></sup> Such claims about other cultures do not necessarily reflect anything about which the author had evidence, but be a form of propaganda or <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a>, similar to <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">blood libel</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Bestiality was accepted in some North American and Middle Eastern indigenous cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Noram_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Noram-53">[53]</a></sup> Sexual intercourse between humans and non-human animals was not uncommon among certain Native American indigenous peoples, including the <a href="/wiki/Hopi" title="Hopi">Hopi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Voget61_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Voget61-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taleyesva_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taleyesva-55">[55]</a></sup> Voget describes the sexual lives of young Native Americans as "rather inclusive," including bestiality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Voget61_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Voget61-54">[54]</a></sup> In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Copper_Inuit" title="Copper Inuit">Copper Inuit</a> people had "no aversion to intercourse with live animals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Voget61_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-Voget61-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several cultures built temples (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khajuraho" title="Khajuraho">Khajuraho</a>, India) or other structures (<a href="/wiki/Sagaholm" title="Sagaholm">Sagaholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">barrow</a>, Sweden) with zoophilic carvings on the exterior, however at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khajuraho" title="Khajuraho">Khajuraho</a> these depictions are not on the interior, perhaps depicting that these are things that belong to the profane world rather than the spiritual world, and thus are to be left outside.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the Church-oriented culture of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> zoophilic activity was met with execution, typically burning, and death to the animals involved either the same way or by hanging, as "both a violation of <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">Biblical edicts</a> and a degradation of man as a spiritual being rather than one that is purely animal and carnal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Some witches were accused of having congress with the devil in the form of an animal. As with all accusations and confessions extracted under torture in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witch_trials_in_Early_Modern_Europe" title="Witch trials in Early Modern Europe">witch trials in Early Modern Europe</a>, their validity cannot be ascertained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BulloughBullough1994_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-BulloughBullough1994-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_perspectives">Religious perspectives</span></h3>
<p>Passages in <a href="/wiki/Leviticus_18" title="Leviticus 18">Leviticus 18</a> (Lev 18:23: "And you shall not lie with any beast and defile yourself with it, neither shall any woman give herself to a beast to lie with it: it is a perversion." RSV) and 20:15–16 ("If a man lies with a beast, he shall be put to death; and you shall kill the beast. If a woman approaches any beast and lies with it, you shall kill the woman and the beast; they shall be put to death, their blood is upon them." RSV) are cited by Jewish, Christian, and Muslim theologians as categorical denunciation of bestiality. However, the teachings of the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a> have been interpreted by some as not expressly forbidding bestiality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plummer_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plummer-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Part II of his <a href="/wiki/Summa_Theologica" title="Summa Theologica">Summa Theologica</a>, medieval philosopher <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> ranked various "unnatural vices" (sex acts resulting in "venereal pleasure" rather than procreation) by degrees of sinfulness, concluding that "the most grievous is the sin of bestiality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Some Christian theologians extend <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Matthew</a>'s view that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antithesis_of_the_Law#Adultery" title="Antithesis of the Law">even having thoughts of adultery is sinful</a> to imply that thoughts of committing bestial acts are likewise sinful.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG/250px-Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG/375px-Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG/500px-Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khajuraho-Lakshmana_Temple_erotic_detal3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Man having intercourse with a horse, pictured on the exterior of a temple in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khajuraho" title="Khajuraho">Khajuraho</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are a few references in <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> scriptures to religious figures engaging in symbolic sexual activity with animals such as explicit depictions of people having sex with animals included amongst the thousands of sculptures of "Life events" on the exterior of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">temple complex</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khajuraho" title="Khajuraho">Khajuraho</a>. The depictions are largely symbolic depictions of the sexualization of some animals and are not meant to be taken literally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> According to the Hindu tradition of erotic painting and sculpture, having sex with an animal is believed to be actually a human having sex with a God incarnated in the form of an animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PodberscekBeetz2005_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-PodberscekBeetz2005-60">[60]</a></sup> However, the Hindu scriptures like the <i><a href="/wiki/Bhagavata_Purana" title="Bhagavata Purana">Bhagavata Purana</a></i> and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devi_Bhagavata_Purana" title="Devi Bhagavata Purana">Devi Bhagavata Purana</a></i> having sex with animals, especially the cow, leads one to <a href="/wiki/Naraka_(Hinduism)" title="Naraka (Hinduism)">Hell</a>, where the person is tormented by rubbing their bodies on trees with razor-sharp thorns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mani_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-mani-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
