<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia_and_the_law" title="Zoophilia and the law">Zoophilia and the law</a></div>
<p>In many jurisdictions, all forms of zoophilic acts are prohibited; others outlaw only the mistreatment of animals, without specific mention of sexual activity. In the UK, <a href="/wiki/Section_63_of_the_Criminal_Justice_and_Immigration_Act_2008" title="Section 63 of the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008">Section 63 of the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008</a> (also known as the Extreme Pornography Act) outlaws images of a person performing or appearing to perform an act of intercourse or oral sex with an animal (whether dead or alive).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opsisect63_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-opsisect63-62">[62]</a></sup> Despite the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice" title="Ministry of Justice">Ministry of Justice</a>'s explanatory note on extreme images saying "It is not a question of the intentions of those who produced the image. Nor is it a question of the sexual arousal of the defendant",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> "it could be argued that a person might possess such an image for the purposes of satire, political commentary or simple grossness," according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Countries such as Belgium and Sweden are somewhere in between: they permit sexual activity with animals, but prohibit the promotion of animal-oriented pornography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Laws on zoophilia are often triggered by specific incidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> While some laws are very specific, others employ vague terms such as "<a href="/wiki/Sodomy" title="Sodomy">sodomy</a>" or "bestiality", which lack legal precision and leave it unclear exactly which acts are covered. In the past, some bestiality laws may have been made in the belief that sex with an animal could result in monstrous offspring, as well as offending the community. Current anti-cruelty laws focus more specifically on animal welfare while anti-bestiality laws are aimed only at offenses to community "standards".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-posner_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-posner-67">[67]</a></sup> Notable legal views include Sweden, where a 2005 report by the Swedish Animal Welfare Agency for the government expressed concern over the increase in reports of <a href="/wiki/Horse-ripping" title="Horse-ripping">horse-ripping</a> incidents. The agency believed current animal cruelty legislation was not sufficient in protecting animals from abuse and needed updating, but concluded that on balance it was not appropriate to call for a ban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, the 1989 Crimes Bill considered abolishing bestiality as a criminal offense, and instead viewing it as a mental health issue, but they did not, and people can still be prosecuted for it. Under Section 143 of the Crimes Act 1961, individuals can serve a sentence of seven years duration for animal sexual abuse and the offence is considered 'complete' in the event of 'penetration'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> a clarification of the anti-bestiality law was made in 2016 which legalizes most forms of sexual contact with animals other than penetration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some countries once had laws against single males living with female animals, such as Alpacas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Copulating with a female alpaca is still specifically against the law in Peru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leavitt2003_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leavitt2003-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2012, bestiality is illegal in 41 U.S. states. Most state bestiality laws were enacted between 1999 and 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TableLaws2016_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-TableLaws2016-74">[74]</a></sup> Until 2005, there was a farm near <a href="/wiki/Enumclaw,_Washington" title="Enumclaw, Washington">Enumclaw, Washington</a> that was described as an “animal brothel”, where people paid to have sex with animals. After <a href="/wiki/Enumclaw_horse_sex_case" title="Enumclaw horse sex case">an incident on 2 July 2005</a>, when a man was pronounced dead in the emergency room of the Enumclaw community hospital after his colon ruptured due to having been sodomized by a horse, the farm garnered police attention. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_Legislature" title="Washington State Legislature">state legislature</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Washington" title="State of Washington">State of Washington</a>, which had been one of the few states in the United States without a law against bestiality, within six months passed a bill making bestiality illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Arizona,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Alaska,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Florida,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Alabama,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> New Jersey<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and New Hampshire<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> have banned sex with animals between 2006 and the present. When such laws are proposed, they are never questioned or debated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Laws which prohibit non-abusive bestiality have been criticized for being discriminatory, unjust and unconstitutional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interdis_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-interdis-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mroberts_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-mroberts-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pornography">Pornography</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Obscenity" title="Obscenity">Obscenity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">Pornography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legal_status_of_Internet_pornography" title="Legal status of Internet pornography">Legal status of Internet pornography</a></div>
<div class="hatnote selfreference">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Animal_pornography" title="Category:Animal pornography">Category:Animal pornography</a>.</div>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="1376" data-file-width="1024" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/30px-Commons-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/45px-Commons-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/59px-Commons-logo.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikimedia Commons has media related to <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Zoophilia_in_art" title="commons:Category:Zoophilia in art">Zoophilia in art</a></b></i>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(28).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="800" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg/300px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg/450px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg/600px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2828%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(28).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Ancient Greek sodomising a goat"</i>, plate XVII from '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Figuris_Veneris" title="De Figuris Veneris">De Figuris Veneris</a>' by F.K. Forberg, illustrated by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril" title="Édouard-Henri Avril">Édouard-Henri Avril</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pornography involving sex with animals is widely illegal, even in most countries where bestiality itself is not explicitly outlawed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, zoophilic pornography would be considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obscene" title="Obscene">obscene</a> if it did not meet the standards of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miller_Test" title="Miller Test">Miller Test</a> and therefore is not openly sold, mailed, distributed or imported across state boundaries or within states which prohibit it. Under U.S. law, 'distribution' includes transmission across the Internet. Production and mere possession appear to be legal, however. U.S. prohibitions on distribution of sexual or obscene materials are as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zoophilia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> in some doubt, having been ruled <a href="/wiki/Constitutionality" title="Constitutionality">unconstitutional</a> in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_v._Extreme_Associates" title="United States v. Extreme Associates">United States v. Extreme Associates</a></i> (a judgement which was overturned on appeal, December 2005).</p>
<p>Similar restrictions apply in Germany (see <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia#Legal_status" title="Zoophilia">above</a>). In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> the possession, making or distribution of material promoting bestiality is illegal.</p>
<p>The potential use of media for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pornographic_movie" title="Pornographic movie">pornographic movies</a> was seen from the start of the era of <a href="/wiki/Silent_film" title="Silent film">silent film</a>. <i>Polissons and Galipettes</i> (re-released 2002 as "<a href="/wiki/The_Good_Old_Naughty_Days" title="The Good Old Naughty Days">The Good Old Naughty Days</a>") is a collection of early French silent films for brothel use, including some animal pornography, dating from around 1905 – 1930.</p>
<p>Material featuring sex with animals is widely available on the Internet, due to their ease of production, and because production and sale is legal in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Prior to the advent of mass-market magazines such as <a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a>, so-called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tijuana_Bible" title="Tijuana Bible">Tijuana Bibles</a> were a form of pornographic tract popular in America, sold as anonymous underground publications typically comprising a small number of stapled comic-strips representing characters and celebrities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The promotion of "stars" began with the Danish <a href="/wiki/Bodil_Joensen" title="Bodil Joensen">Bodil Joensen</a>, in the period of 1969–72, along with other porn actors such as the Americans <a href="/wiki/Linda_Lovelace" title="Linda Lovelace">Linda Lovelace</a> (<i>Dogarama</i>, 1969), Chessie Moore (multiple films, c. 1994), Kerri Downs (three films, 1998) and Calina Lynx (aka Kelly G'raffe) (two films, 1998). Another early film to attain great infamy was "<a href="/wiki/Animal_Farm_(video)" title="Animal Farm (video)">Animal Farm</a>", smuggled into Great Britain around 1980 without details as to makers or provenance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The film was later traced to a crude juxtaposition of smuggled cuts from many of Bodil Joensen's 1970s Danish movies.</p>
<p>Into the 1980s the Dutch took the lead, creating figures like "Wilma" and the "Dutch Sisters". In 1980s, "bestiality" was featured in Italian adult films with actresses like Denise Dior, Francesca Ray, and <a href="/wiki/Marina_Hedman" title="Marina Hedman">Marina Hedman</a>, manifested early in the softcore flick <i>Bestialità</i> in 1976.</p>
<p>Today, in <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, where production faces no legal limitations, zoophilic materials have become a substantial industry that produces numerous films and magazines, particularly for Dutch companies such as <i>Topscore</i> and <i>Book &amp; Film International</i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Genre" title="Genre">genre</a> has stars such as "Hector", a <a href="/wiki/Great_Dane" title="Great Dane">Great Dane</a> starring in several films. Many Hungarian mainstream performers also appeared anonymously in animal pornography in their early careers. For example, Suzy Spark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Japan, animal pornography is used to bypass censorship laws, often featuring Japanese and Swedish female models performing <a href="/wiki/Fellatio" title="Fellatio">fellatio</a> on animals, because oral penetration of a non-human penis is not in the scope of Japanese mosaic censor. <a href="/wiki/Sakura_Sakurada" title="Sakura Sakurada">Sakura Sakurada</a> is an <a href="/wiki/AV_idol" title="AV idol">AV idol</a> known to have appeared in animal pornography, specifically in the AV <i>The Dog Game</i> in 2006. While primarily underground, there are a number of animal pornography actresses who specialize in bestiality movies. A box-office success of the 1980s, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/24_Horas_de_Sexo_Expl%C3%ADcito" title="24 Horas de Sexo Explícito">24 Horas de Sexo Explícito</a></i> featured zoophilia.</p>
<p>In the UK <a href="/wiki/Section_63_of_the_Criminal_Justice_and_Immigration_Act_2008" title="Section 63 of the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008">Section 63 of the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008</a> criminalises possession of realistic pornographic images depicting sex with animals (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_pornography" title="Extreme pornography">extreme pornography</a>), including fake images and simulated acts, as well as images depicting sex with dead animals, where no crime has taken place in the production. The law provides for sentences of up to two years in prison; a sentence of 12 months was handed down in one case in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pornography of this sort has become the business of certain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spam_(electronic)" title="Spam (electronic)">spammers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jaynes" title="Jeremy Jaynes">Jeremy Jaynes</a> and owners of some fake <a href="/wiki/Thumbnail_gallery_post" title="Thumbnail gallery post">TGPs</a>, who use the promise of "extreme" material as a bid for users' attention.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_safety">Health and safety</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia_and_health" title="Zoophilia and health">Zoophilia and health</a></div>
<p>Infections that are transmitted from animals to humans are called <a href="/wiki/Zoonosis" title="Zoonosis">zoonoses</a>. Some zoonoses may be transferred through casual contact, but others are much more readily transferred by activities that expose humans to the <a href="/wiki/Semen" title="Semen">semen</a>, vaginal fluids, <a href="/wiki/Urine" title="Urine">urine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saliva" title="Saliva">saliva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feces" title="Feces">feces</a> and blood of animals. Examples of zoonoses are <a href="/wiki/Brucellosis" title="Brucellosis">Brucellosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q_fever" title="Q fever">Q fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leptospirosis" title="Leptospirosis">leptospirosis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toxocariasis" title="Toxocariasis">toxocariasis</a>. Therefore, sexual activity with animals is, in some instances, a high risk activity. <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">Allergic reactions</a> to animal semen may occur, including <a href="/wiki/Anaphylaxis" title="Anaphylaxis">anaphylaxis</a>. Bites and other trauma from penetration or trampling may occur.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoophiles">Zoophiles</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-sexual_zoophilia">Non-sexual zoophilia</span></h3>
<p>The love of animals is not necessarily sexual in nature. In <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> the word "zoophilia" is sometimes used without sexual implications. Being fond of animals in general, or as pets, is accepted in Western society, and is usually respected or tolerated. However, the word zoophilia is used to mean a sexual preference towards animals, which makes it <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CraigheadNemeroff2002_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-CraigheadNemeroff2002-91">[91]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilia</a>. Some zoophiles may not act on their sexual attraction to animals. People who identify as zoophiles may feel their love for animals is romantic rather than purely sexual, and say this makes them different from those committing entirely sexually motivated acts of bestiality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delaney2003_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delaney2003-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoophile_community">Zoophile community</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2545" data-file-width="2688" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg/220px-Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg/330px-Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg/440px-Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zeta_toy_MMB_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Several companies (e.g., Bad Dragon) sell <a href="/wiki/Dildo" title="Dildo">dildos</a> in the shape of animal penises, both realistic and fantastical. This one is based on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolf%27s_penis" title="Wolf's penis">wolf's penis</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An online survey which recruited participants over the internet concluded that prior to the arrival of widespread <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">computer networking</a>, most zoophiles would not have known other zoophiles, and for the most part, zoophiles engaged in bestiality secretly, or told only trusted friends, family or partners. The internet and its predecessors made people able to search for information on topics which were not otherwise easily accessible and to communicate with relative safety and anonymity. Because of the diary-like intimacy of blogs and the anonymity of the internet, zoophiles had the ideal opportunity to "openly" express their sexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> As with many other <a href="/wiki/Alternative_lifestyle" title="Alternative lifestyle">alternate lifestyles</a>, broader networks began forming in the 1980s when participating in <a href="/wiki/Online_community" title="Online community">networked social groups</a> became more common at home and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberg_and_Williams_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberg_and_Williams-94">[94]</a></sup> Such developments in general were described by Markoff in 1990; the linking of computers meant that people thousands of miles apart could feel the intimacy akin to being in a small village together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The popular newsgroup <a href="/wiki/Alt.sex" title="Alt.sex">alt.sex.bestiality</a>, said to be in the top 1% of newsgroup interest (i.e. number 50 out of around 5000), – and reputedly started in humor<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> – along with personal <a href="/wiki/Bulletin_board" title="Bulletin board">bulletin boards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Talker" title="Talker">talkers</a>, chief among them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleepy%27s_multiple_worlds" title="Sleepy's multiple worlds">Sleepy's multiple worlds</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lintilla_(talker)" title="Lintilla (talker)">Lintilla</a>, and Planes of Existence, were among the first group media of this kind in the late 1980s and early 1990s. These groups rapidly drew together zoophiles, some of whom also created personal and social websites and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_Forum" title="Internet Forum">internet forums</a>. By around 1992–1994, the wide social net had evolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> This was initially centered around the above-mentioned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newsgroup" title="Newsgroup">newsgroup</a>, alt.sex.bestiality, which during the six years following 1990 had matured into a discussion and support group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The newsgroup included information about health issues, laws governing zoophilia, bibliography relating to the subject, and community events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Since the 1990s, other zoophile websites have been created and have grown in size; for example, the zoophile website and internet forum "beastforum.com" has more than one million members as of March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Weinberg and Williams observe that the internet can socially integrate an incredibly large number of people. In Kinsey’s day contacts between animal lovers were more localized and limited to male compatriots in a particular rural community. Further, while the farm boys Kinsey researched might have been part of a rural culture in which sex with animals was a part, the sex itself did not define the community. The zoophile community is not known to be particularly large compared to other subcultures which make use of the internet, so Weinberg and Williams surmised its aims and beliefs would likely change little as it grew. Those particularly active on the internet may not be aware of a wider subculture, as there is not much of a wider subculture<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, Weinberg and Williams felt the virtual zoophile group would lead the development of the subculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberg_and_Williams_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberg_and_Williams-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>There also exist websites which aim to provide support and social assistance to zoophiles (including resources to help and rescue abused or mistreated animals), but these are not usually well publicized. Such work is often undertaken as needed by individuals and friends, within social networks, and by word of mouth. One notable early attempt at creating a zoophile support structure focused on social and psychological support was the newsgroup soc.support.zoophilia, which was proposed in 1994 but narrowly failed to meet the 2/3 majority needed to be created<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. There was also a German support group called "Interessengemeinschaft Zoophiler Menschen ("Zoophile Interest Group").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zoophiles tend to experience their first zoosexual feelings during adolescence, and tend to be secretive about it, hence limiting the ability for non-Internet communities to form:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-browplm2_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-browplm2-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"I asked him [a zoophile] when he had his first inkling of being a zoophile. 'When you're a kid, you're not really aware of too much sexually,' he says. 'But I was always interested in animals, starting around age 10. It was an extension of my affection for the dog and of my discovery of sex. He's a male. I'm a male. I wanted to make him feel good.' His attraction to dogs became stronger in his teens and stronger yet in his 20s. 'For years, I thought I was the only one who did this,' James says. 'I felt like there was no one I could talk to about this. I definitely knew I wasn't going to be talking to my parents or my friends about this.'[...] 'This is not a fetish,' James says of his attractions. 'It's an orientation, a lifestyle.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-browplm2_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-browplm2-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Debate_over_zoophilia_or_zoophilic_relations">Debate over zoophilia or zoophilic relations</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="677" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg/220px-Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg/330px-Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg/440px-Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leda_-_after_Michelangelo_Buonarroti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Leda_and_the_Swan" title="Leda and the Swan">Leda and the Swan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because of its controversial nature, people have developed arguments both for<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singer01_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-singer01-107">[107]</a></sup> and against<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> zoophilia. Arguments for and against zoosexual activity from a variety of sources, including religious, moral, ethical, psychological, medical and social.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arguments_against_bestiality">Arguments against bestiality</span></h3>
<p>Bestiality is seen by the government of the United Kingdom as profoundly disturbed behavior (as indicated by the UK <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> review on sexual offences in 2002).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Andrea Beetz states there is evidence that there can be violent zoosadistic approaches to sex with animals. Beetz argues that animals might be traumatized even by a non-violent, sexual approach from a human;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8-110">[110]</a></sup> however, Beetz also says that in some cases, non-abusive bestiality can be reciprocally pleasurable for both the human and non-human animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>An argument from human dignity is given by Wesley J. Smith, a senior fellow and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligent_Design" title="Intelligent Design">Intelligent Design</a> proponent at the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Science_and_Culture" title="Center for Science and Culture">Center for Science and Culture</a> of the conservative Christian <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Institute" title="Discovery Institute">Discovery Institute</a>: – "such behavior is profoundly degrading and utterly subversive to the crucial understanding that human beings are unique, special, and of the highest moral worth in the known universe—a concept known as '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_exceptionalism" title="Human exceptionalism">human exceptionalism</a>' ... one of the reasons bestiality is condemned through law is that such degrading conduct unacceptably subverts standards of basic human dignity and is an affront to humankind's inestimable importance and intrinsic moral worth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the primary critiques of bestiality is that it is harmful to animals and necessarily abusive, because animals are unable to give or withhold consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regan63_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Regan63-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humane_Society_of_the_United_States" title="Humane Society of the United States">Humane Society of the United States</a> (HSUS) has said that as animals do not have the same capacity for thinking as humans, they are unable to give full consent. The HSUS takes the position that all sexual activity between humans and animals is abusive, whether it involves physical injury or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In his 1993 article, Dr. Frank Ascione stated that "bestiality may be considered abusive even in cases when physical harm to an animal does not occur." In a 1997 article, Piers Beirne, Professor of Criminology at the University of Southern Maine, points out that 'for genuine consent to sexual relations to be present...both participants must be conscious, fully informed and positive in their desires.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arguments_for_bestiality">Arguments for bestiality</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Book_with_sexual_content_15th_century_Iran_003_cr.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="299" height="405" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Book_with_sexual_content_15th_century_Iran_003_cr.jpg/220px-Book_with_sexual_content_15th_century_Iran_003_cr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/Book_with_sexual_content_15th_century_Iran_003_cr.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Book_with_sexual_content_15th_century_Iran_003_cr.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Book illustration depicting dog with woman, <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, 15th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some defenders of bestiality argue that the issue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_consent" title="Sexual consent">sexual consent</a> is irrelevant because many legal human practices (such as <a href="/wiki/Semen_collection" title="Semen collection">semen collection</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination_of_livestock_and_pets" title="Artificial insemination of livestock and pets">artificial insemination</a>, hunting, <a href="/wiki/Animal_testing" title="Animal testing">laboratory testing</a>, and slaughtering animals for meat) do not involve the consent of the animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Brian Cutteridge states the following regarding this argument:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Animal sexual autonomy is regularly violated for human financial gain through procedures such as [artificial insemination and slaughter]. Such procedures are probably more disturbing physically and psychologically than acts of zoophilia would be, yet the issue of consent on the part of the animal is never raised in the discussion of such procedures. To confine the 'right' of any animal strictly to acts of zoophilia is thus to make a law [against zoophilia] based not on reason but on moral prejudice, and to breach the constitutional rights of zoophiles to due process and equality before the law. [...] Laws which criminalize zoophilia based on societal abhorrence of such acts rather than any real harm caused by such acts are an unjust and unconstitutional infringement on individual liberty."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interdis_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-interdis-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hani_Miletski" title="Hani Miletski">Miletski</a> believes that "Animals are capable of sexual consent – and even initiation – in their own way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> It is not an uncommon practice for dogs to attempt to copulate with ("hump") the legs of people of both genders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Rosenberger (1968) emphasizes that as far as cunnilingus is concerned, dogs require no training, and even Dekkers (1994) and Menninger (1951) admit that sometimes animals take the initiative and do so impulsively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-Beetz_2002.2C_section_5.2.8-110">[110]</a></sup> Those supporting zoophilic activity feel animals sometimes even seem to enjoy the sexual attention<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> or voluntarily initiate sexual activity with humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dekkers.2C_1994_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dekkers.2C_1994-120">[120]</a></sup> Animals such as dogs can be willing participants in sexual activity with humans, and "seem to enjoy the attention provided by the sexual interaction with a human."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interdis_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-interdis-85">[85]</a></sup> Animal owners normally know what their own pets like or do not like. Most people can tell if an animal does not like how it is being petted, because it will move away. An animal that is liking being petted pushes against the hand, and seems to enjoy it. To those defending bestiality this is seen as a way in which animals give consent, or the fact that a dog might wag its tail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Preference_utilitarianism" title="Preference utilitarianism">Utilitarian</a> philosopher and <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal liberation</a> author <a href="/wiki/Peter_Singer" title="Peter Singer">Peter Singer</a> argues that bestiality is not unethical so long as it involves no harm or cruelty to the animal<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SingerNerve_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-SingerNerve-122">[122]</a></sup> (see <i><a href="/wiki/Harm_principle" title="Harm principle">Harm principle</a></i>). In the article "Heavy Petting,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singer01_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singer01-123">[123]</a></sup> Singer argues that zoosexual activity need not be abusive, and that relationships could form which were mutually enjoyed. Singer and others have argued that people's dislike of bestiality is partly caused by irrational <a href="/wiki/Speciesism" title="Speciesism">speciesism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropocentrism" title="Anthropocentrism">anthropocentrism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Because interspecies sex occurs in nature,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> and because humans <i>are</i> animals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> supporters argue that zoosexual activity is not "unnatural" and is not intrinsically wrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mroberts_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-mroberts-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research has proven that non-human animals can and do have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_co-opted_sexual_behavior" title="Animal co-opted sexual behavior">sex for non-reproductive purposes</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Animal_sexual_behaviour#Sex_for_pleasure" title="Animal sexual behaviour">for pleasure</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Poiani_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Poiani-129">[129]</a></sup> In 2006, a Danish Animal Ethics Council report concluded that ethically performed zoosexual activity is capable of providing a positive experience for all participants, and that some non-human animals are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_imprinting" title="Sexual imprinting">sexually attracted to humans</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> (for example, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolphins" title="Dolphins">dolphins</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mentions_in_the_media">Mentions in the media</span></h2>
<p>Because of its controversial nature, different countries vary in the discussion of bestiality. Often sexual matters are the subject of legal or regulatory requirement. In 2005 the UK broadcasting regulator (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OFCOM" title="OFCOM">OFCOM</a>) updated its code stating that freedom of expression is at the heart of any democratic state. Adult audiences should be informed as to what they will be viewing or hearing, and the young, who cannot make a fully informed choice for themselves, should be protected. Hence a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watershed_(television)" title="Watershed (television)">watershed</a> and other precautions were set up for explicit sexual material, to protect young people. Zoophile activity and other sexual matters may be discussed, but only in an appropriate context and manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IPT was replaced after the Films, Videos, and Publications Classification Act in 1993, replaced with bodies designed to allow both more debate and increased consistency, and possession and supply of material that it is decided are objectionable was made a criminal offence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mention in the media is often comical in nature. References to bestiality are not uncommon in some media, especially adult <a href="/wiki/Cartoon" title="Cartoon">cartoon</a> series such as <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Satire" title="Satire">satirical comedy</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Borat" title="Borat">Borat</a></i>, and films (especially shock <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_film" title="Exploitation film">exploitation films</a>), although a few broadcasters such as <a href="/wiki/Howard_Stern" title="Howard Stern">Howard Stern</a> (who joked about bestiality dial-a-date on NBC) and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Binns" title="Tom Binns">Tom Binns</a> (whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XFM_London" title="XFM London">XFM London</a> Breakfast Show resulted on one occasion in a live discussion about the ethics of zoophilic pornographic movies at peak child listening time) have been reprimanded by their stations for doing so.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In literature, American novelist <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a> refers to a photo of a woman attempting sexual intercourse with a Shetland Pony in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sirens_of_Titan" title="The Sirens of Titan">The Sirens of Titan</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slaughterhouse_Five" title="Slaughterhouse Five">Slaughterhouse Five</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/God_Bless_You,_Mr._Rosewater" title="God Bless You, Mr. Rosewater">God Bless You, Mr. Rosewater</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Philip_K._Dick" title="Philip K. Dick">Philip K. Dick</a> also refers to a photo of a woman copulating with a Shetland Pony in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flow_My_Tears_The_Policeman_Said" title="Flow My Tears The Policeman Said">Flow My Tears The Policeman Said</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/John_Irving" title="John Irving">John Irving</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cider_House_Rules" title="The Cider House Rules">The Cider House Rules</a></i> repeatedly mentions a pornographic photograph depicting oral sex on a pony. In <i><a href="/wiki/Clerks_II" title="Clerks II">Clerks II</a></i> Randal orders a <a href="/wiki/Donkey_show" title="Donkey show">donkey show</a> as a going away present for his best friend Dante, in which it is referred to as "interspecies erotica" by the male performer.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pu_Songling" title="Pu Songling">Pu Songling</a> refers to zoophilia in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strange_Tales_from_a_Chinese_Studio" title="Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio">Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio</a></i> short story "<a href="/wiki/The_Fornicating_Dog" title="The Fornicating Dog">The Fornicating Dog</a>", which talks about sexual relations between a woman and her white dog.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film.2C_television_and_radio">Film, television and radio</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i>Animal passions</i> (part of the Hidden Love series) (1999, follow-up sequel 2004, Channel 4, UK): Ofcom [the UK television regulator] reported that: "This was a serious documentary exploring a rare minority sexual orientation. Although the programme gave an opportunity for zoophiles to express their opinions, the effect was neither to sensationalise nor normalise their behaviour."</li>
<li><i>Sexe et confidences</i> (April 2002, CBSC Decision C01/02-329, Canada): Hour-long sex information program hosted by sexologist Louise-Andrée Saulnier discussing zoophilia. Covered folklore, academic studies and general information, plus telephone call-in from viewers describing their zoophilic experiences and stories they had heard.</li>
<li><i>Talk Sport Radio</i> (December 2002, UK): Live talkshow interview with lifelong zoophile, followed by call-in discussion.</li>
<li><i>Animal Love</i> (1995, Ulrich Seidl, Austria)</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoo_(movie)" title="Zoo (movie)">Zoo</a></i> (2007), a documentary of the life and death of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenneth_Pinyan" title="Kenneth Pinyan">Kenneth Pinyan</a>, and those who came to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enumclaw" title="Enumclaw">Enumclaw</a> for a similar reason. One of 16 out of 856 candidates awarded a place at the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> 2007.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Dogs_Lie_(2006_film)" title="Sleeping Dogs Lie (2006 film)">Sleeping Dogs Lie</a></i> (also known as <i>'Stay'</i>): A romantic comedy in which a girl's engagement is heavily tested when she confesses to her <a href="/wiki/Engagement" title="Engagement">fiance</a> that when younger she performed <a href="/wiki/Oral_sex" title="Oral sex">oral sex</a> on her dog.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Vase_de_Noces" title="Vase de Noces">Vase de Noces</a></i>, a controversial <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Belgium" title="Cinema of Belgium">Belgian</a> art film about the disturbing sexual relationship between a man and his pig.</li>
</ul>
